  <raw>AUTOMOTIVE SUPPLIER DENSO TO CARRY OUT EUR 95 MILLION CAPACITY



AUTOMOTIVE  SUPPLIER  DENSO TO CARRY  OUT  EUR  95  MILLION  CAPACITY
EXPANSION
Denso  Hungary  Kft, a subsidiary of Japanese automotive supplier  Denso
Corporation,  is  carrying  out a EUR 95 million  investment  to  expand
component manufacturing capacities in the city of Szekesfehervar.
The  investment  will  be  supported with a EUR 9.5  million  government
grant.

  The  aid  was granted by the economy ministry on  an  individual
basis,  a form of support that is available for large firms who plan  to
carry  out investments exceeding EUR 50 million. This new, EU-compatible
support form was first applied to electronics manufacturer Bosch,  which
signed a EUR 15 million support agreement last week.
Construction of Denso's new facilities will be completed at the  end  of
August. The company will manufacture diesel fuel pumps that will be used
in  Ford  and Fiat engines. The new factories will employ 1100  workers,
taking  the  number of workers at Denso Hungary to 2500 by  the  end  of
2005.
As  a  result  of  the  investment, Denso Hungary's sales  revenues  are
expected  to rise from EUR 133 million last year to EUR 320  million  by
2006.  Currently, the company's major clients are Toyota, Isuzu, Nissan,
Volkswagen  and  Audi,  but  the  Hungarian  subsidiary  also   delivers
components  used  in Land Rover, Ford, Jaguar, Peugeot  and  Lamborghini
cars.
The output of Hungary's automotive industry totaled USD 8.46 billion  in
2003,  and  accounted for 15% of all manufacturing in Hungary, according
to   the   ministry's   figures.  Within  this,   automotive   component
manufacturers recorded sales approaching USD 1.5 billion. In all, 13  of
the world's 30 largest automotive suppliers are present in Hungary.
Of  cars assembled in Hungary, 94.3% are exported, while exports account
for  87.6%  of  the  automotive components industry,  according  to  the
ministry.</raw>
